<text>Came here for Wine Wednesday and had a blast on the happy hour specials... enjoyed some vino and the boilermakers (Pilsner + Bourbon)... my friend had a classy gin based well and lavish pizza bread.... she was in love with it... as most pizza lovers are...

The Oak and Vine is a very mood lit... has great music and even better service.

They do wine flight specials after 9pm and have a vegan option or two on the menu. A lot of stuff can be made vegan or is vegan friendly, but they don't have a major item aside from olives.

Parking is pretty decent and nearby as there are a couple shared lots that are extremely walkable... street p is rare... but they don't validate.

Overall recommend this place for any type of hang as they have ales, brew and beverages of all kinds.</text>< Rating>

< text>
Stopped in recently after a long time away and feel back in love with the Oak and Vine.

A party for six quickly turned into a party for two with all the holiday traffic, but there is parking very close by in a structure unfortunately O & V don't validate.

This wine bar bistro has amazing ambience a great happy hour and lots of pairing eats. Not many vegan options (sigh) but some things that can be made vegan friendly with a heads up.

Drinks are stiff however wonderful. We had amazing service (Ben is the best) and mostly great drinks not a fan of the house red (Cupcake) but do love their wine flight special after 9pm.

Definitely make a reservation if you're in a large party as seating inside and on the patio is limited and they will and want to accommodate you.<//text>

<Text>We found this place, close to the main street and decided to check it out. It was getting late and a few other spots were too busy or already closed. Lovely restaurant!! The food was excellent. We had a vegetable and goat cheese ravioli and the cioppino. Both were so incredibly tasty with wonderful, full flavors. They actually had an impressively large menu with many options that all looked amazing. I was also very impressed by the excellent service. Due to Covid, there was only outdoor patio dining. They had heat lamps but our particular table was by the door of the restaurant so it was far away from a lamp. I was getting chilly so my bf went to the car to get me a jacket. I really didn't make a fuss about it, and didn't think anyone noticed, but very soon after that (literally one minute after my bf got up), an owner/manager came over and asked if I would like them to move our table closer to the heat lamp. The other tables were all taken so they physically had to transport the table over. It was much more comfortable under the heat lamp, and I had a great night, but most of all, I was so impressed that they guessed what I needed without me even saying a word! Very thoughtful. All the staff were so friendly and professional. I would love to go back in the future to try more of the menu items. It's located right in downtown Carmel so there is a really lovely, romantic vibe to the place.</text>

</record></dataset><record>
<Text>What an unexpectedly special dinner.

Arrived without reservations on a Wednesday night. The hostess (whose name I unfortunately did not get - it was her first night and she was fabulous) sat me at the "single diner table" - you know the one: under the spotlight, next to the hostess stand, just outside the door.

15 minutes without water or introduction and I was considering going elsewhere, but then the magic started.

The server (who said her name but I failed to write it down and thus had no chance of remembering) recommended her favorite Cabernet and, being more in the mood to drink wine than to be picky, I quickly agreed to it.

I ordered one of the specials for an app and the beef ravioli along with the hastily agreed upon vino.

This wine. Ladies and gentlemen (and anyone in between or outside of gender duality). It is something special. It is Block 57, and produced by the owner of the bistro. I'll let you look up the cheeky story behind it for yourselves, as I did. It's, as Firok (said owner) put it and I agree, "something special." I ended up needing a bottle to take home. And I really will save it for something special, not drink it alone in quarantine with Netflix. It deserves better than that.

I tried another wine - the Sirah, I believe it was - which I exclaimed to be "as if someone deftly shook out a lightweight velvet blanket and settled it gently over the tongue". More specialness.

The food was spectacular. (And I'm one of those annoying restaurant industry people.) Scallops cooked perfectly, their sauce just rich enough to warrant soup sized spoonfuls but not so rich as to eclipse the lightness of the tender medallions themselves. The ravioli was PERFECTION. I won't gross you out with all the times I've had pasta in Italy blah blah blah. Just ORDER IT. And get, as Firok rightly suggested, more parmesan grated on top than you feel is proper. I scraped the dish as clean as I could get it.

It's always special when the owner is present and their presence ADDS to the experience (you know what it's like when it's the opposite... shudder). This was a fantastic experience. I left feeling happy to be alive.

Thank you Firok and staff. Can't wait to come back.< /Text><userid>106338409012855706548</userid>< rate>
5<//rate>

4<//Rate>
<Text>Dog-friendly Carmel classic. Does everything well; many places do some things better, but don't do other things at all, or not-so-pretty-good. They have managed to avoid the 'all things to all people' trap, while appealing to a wide spectrum of tastes. Have I had better cioppino? Sure. But can I get a perfectly nice cioppino AND my dining partner a really good steak? Here, yes. (BTW, I have had wretched cioppino at 2X the price in San Francisco.)
I live in CA,  so I am inundated with CA wines. The wine cellar is heavy on California wines, very many proprietary and brilliant. It is extremely important for an international tourist destination to feature this. I might prefer a little Greco de Tufo or a Super-Tuscan, but reviewing this as a 'Local Guide', you will get my personal impression. I am not the chamber of commerce. That said, I was able to choose perfectly acceptable pairings.
Giovanni offers satisfying portions at a reasonable price; it and the wine list are value-for-money. They apparently offer Block 57 propriety wines for off-sale which I am not prepared to review. For this I apologise.
Service above average. Lots of ice cubes for our doggies.< /Text><Pics>None</Pics><response>None</response><GmapID>0x808de66b2a01fb19:0xc16a56a13a23c99f</GmapID></record></dataset><record>
